title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Crosstown_Classic">Crosstown Classic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Crosstown Classic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:West_Side_Grounds_1905.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/West_Side_Grounds_1905.jpg/220px-West_Side_Grounds_1905.jpg" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/West_Side_Grounds_1905.jpg/330px-West_Side_Grounds_1905.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/West_Side_Grounds_1905.jpg/440px-West_Side_Grounds_1905.jpg 2x" data-file-width="633" data-file-height="330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:West_Side_Grounds_1905.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fielder Jones of the White Sox hits the ball against Cubs at West Side Grounds, 1905</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cubs%E2%80%93White_Sox_rivalry" title="Cubs\xe2\x80\x93White Sox rivalry">Cubs\xe2\x80\x93White Sox rivalry</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Cubs%E2%80%93White_Sox_rivalry" title="Cubs\xe2\x80\x93White Sox rivalry">crosstown rivals</a> of the White Sox, a rivalry that some made fun of prior to the White Sox\'s 2005 title because both of them had extremely long championship droughts. The nature of the rivalry is unique; with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/1906_World_Series" title="1906 World Series">1906 World Series</a>, in which the White Sox upset the favored Cubs, the teams never met in an official game until <a href="/wiki/1997_in_baseball" title="1997 in baseball">1997</a>, when interleague play was introduced. In the intervening time, the two teams sometimes met for exhibition games. The White Sox currently lead the regular season series 48\xe2\x80\x9339, winning the last 4 seasons in a row. The BP Crosstown Cup was introduced in 2010 and the White Sox won the first three seasons (2010-2012) until the Cubs first won the Cup in 2013 by sweeping the season series.  The White Sox won the Cup the next season and retained the Cup the following two years (series was a tie - Cup remains with defending team in the event of a tie).  The Cubs took back the Cup in 2017.  There have been two series sweeps since interleague play began both by the Cubs: 1998 and 2013.\n</p><p>An example of this volatile rivalry is the game played between the White Sox and the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> at U.S. Cellular Field on May 20, <a href="/wiki/2006_in_baseball" title="2006 in baseball">2006</a>. White Sox catcher <a href="/wiki/A._J._Pierzynski" title="A. J. Pierzynski">A. J. Pierzynski</a> was running home on a sacrifice fly by center fielder <a href="/wiki/Brian_Anderson_(outfielder)" title="Brian Anderson (outfielder)">Brian Anderson</a> and smashed into Cubs catcher <a href="/wiki/Michael_Barrett_(baseball)" title="Michael Barrett (baseball)">Michael Barrett</a>, who was blocking home plate. Pierzynski lost his helmet in the collision, and slapped the plate as he rose. Barrett stopped him and, after exchanging a few words, punched Pierzynski in the face, causing a melee to ensue. Brian Anderson and Cubs first baseman <a href="/wiki/John_Mabry" title="John Mabry">John Mabry</a> got involved in a separate confrontation, although it was later determined that Mabry was attempting to be a peacemaker. After 10 minutes of conferring following the fight, the umpires ejected Pierzynski, Barrett, Anderson, and Mabry. As Pierzynski entered his dugout, he pumped his arms, causing the soldout crowd at U.S. Cellular Field to erupt in cheers. When play resumed, White Sox second baseman <a href="/wiki/Tadahito_Iguchi" title="Tadahito Iguchi">Tadahito Iguchi</a> blasted a grand slam to put the White Sox up 5\xe2\x80\x930 on their way to a 7\xe2\x80\x930 win over their crosstown rivals. While there are other major league cities and metropolitan areas in which two teams co-exist, all of the others feature at least one team which began playing there in <a href="/wiki/1961_in_baseball" title="1961 in baseball">1961</a> or later, whereas the White Sox and Cubs have been competing for their city\'s fans since 1901.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisional">Divisional</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Divisional">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_rivalries#Chicago_White_Sox_vs._Detroit_Tigers" title="Major League Baseball rivalries">Major League Baseball rivalries \xc2\xa7&#160;Chicago White Sox vs. Detroit Tigers</a></div>\n<p>The White Sox enjoy healthy divisional rivalries. The <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a> are one of Chicago\'s primary rivals, and the cities of Chicago and Detroit share rivalries in other sports as well, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bulls%E2%80%93Pistons_rivalry" title="Bulls\xe2\x80\x93Pistons rivalry">Bulls\xe2\x80\x93Pistons rivalry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackhawks%E2%80%93Red_Wings_rivalry" title="Blackhawks\xe2\x80\x93Red Wings rivalry">Blackhawks\xe2\x80\x93Red Wings rivalry</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bears%E2%80%93Lions_rivalry" title="Bears\xe2\x80\x93Lions rivalry">Bears\xe2\x80\x93Lions rivalry</a>. The rivalry has had its fair share of fights as well. The two teams are separated by a small under 5 hour drive, leading to fans of both teams showing up in large numbers at each others home stadiums. The teams have also got into a number of brawls, the most famous of which occurred in 2000 along with "binocular-gate" in 2014. In 2016, Al Avila, the GM of the Tigers let his own son, catcher Alex Avila, leave the Tigers to sign with the White Sox. \n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_rivalries#Chicago_White_Sox_vs._Minnesota_Twins" title="Major League Baseball rivalries">Major League Baseball rivalries \xc2\xa7&#160;Chicago White Sox vs. Minnesota Twins</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a> are high-profile rivals as well, with fans of both teams showing up to Comiskey Park and Target Field in healthy numbers. The White Sox and Twins also played in a one-game playoff in <a href="/wiki/2008_American_League_Central_tie-breaker_game" title="2008 American League Central tie-breaker game">2008</a>, the White Sox would win the game 1\xe2\x80\x930 and the division. Between 2000 and 2010 the teams combined for 9 AL Central titles, and although the Twins won 6 times to the White Sox 3, the White Sox won the only world series of the two in this time (2005). Former all-star catcher A.J. Pierzynski played for both teams and left Minnesota in 2003 and join the Sox in 2005, he received boos on his first visit back to Minnesota. \n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_rivalries#Chicago_White_Sox_vs._Cleveland_Indians" title="Major League Baseball rivalries">Major League Baseball rivalries \xc2\xa7&#160;Chicago White Sox vs. Cleveland Indians</a></div>\n<p>Chicago has another rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>. The rivalry first started upon the creation of the AL Central in 1994. On July 15, 1994 an umpire confiscated <a href="/wiki/Albert_Belle" title="Albert Belle">Albert Belle</a>\'s bat, presuming that it was corked. They put it in the umpire\'s room at Comiskey Park. However, Indians pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jason_Grimsley" title="Jason Grimsley">Jason Grimsley</a> climbed through the ceiling from the visitor\'s clubhouse and stole the bat. The theft was discovered and Belle was suspended; Grimsley later owned up to the theft. Belle further inflamed matters by spurning the Indians and signing a large free agent contract with the White Sox in 1997. In 2005, during the White Sox world series chase, the Indians cut down the Sox lead in the division from 14 games to 3 heading into the final weekend of the season with the Sox at 96-63 and the Tribe at 93-66, the White Sox swept the Indians and knocked them both out of the division race and wild card hunt with mostly back up players.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical">Historical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Historical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A historical regional rival was the St. Louis Browns. Through the 1953 season, the two teams were located fairly close to each other (including the 1901 season when the Browns were the Milwaukee Brewers), and could have been seen as the American League equivalent of the <a href="/wiki/Cardinals%E2%80%93Cubs_rivalry" title="Cardinals\xe2\x80\x93Cubs rivalry">Cardinals\xe2\x80\x93Cubs rivalry</a>, being that Chicago and St. Louis have for years been connected by the same highway (<a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_66" title="U.S. Route 66">U.S. Route 66</a> and now <a href="/wiki/Interstate_55" title="Interstate 55">Interstate 55</a>). The rivalry has been somewhat revived at times in the past, involving the Browns\' current identity, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>, most notably in 1983.\n</p><p>The current <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> franchise were arguably the White Sox main and biggest rival, due to the proximity of the two cities (resulting in large numbers of White Sox fans who would regularly be in attendance at the Brewers former home <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_County_Stadium" title="Milwaukee County Stadium">Milwaukee County Stadium</a>), and with the teams competing in the same American League division for the 1970 and 1971 seasons and then again from 1994 to 1997. The rivalry has since cooled off however, when the Brewers moved to the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> in 1998.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting">Broadcasting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Broadcasting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chicago_White_Sox_broadcasters" title="List of Chicago White Sox broadcasters">List of Chicago White Sox broadcasters</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bob_Elson_circa_1940s.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Bob_Elson_circa_1940s.JPG/150px-Bob_Elson_circa_1940s.JPG" width="150" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Bob_Elson_circa_1940s.JPG/225px-Bob_Elson_circa_1940s.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Bob_Elson_circa_1940s.JPG/300px-Bob_Elson_circa_1940s.JPG 2x" data-file-width="710" data-file-height="921" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bob_Elson_circa_1940s.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Elson in the 1940s.</div></div></div>\n<p>The White Sox did not sell exclusive rights for radio broadcasts from radio\'s inception until 1944, instead having local stations share rights for games, and after <a href="/wiki/WGN_(AM)" title="WGN (AM)">WGN</a> (720) was forced to abdicate their rights to the team in the 1943 after sixteen seasons due to children\'s programming commitments from their network, <a href="/wiki/Mutual_Broadcasting_System" title="Mutual Broadcasting System">Mutual</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cbmradio_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbmradio-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The White Sox first granted exclusive rights in 1944, and would bounce between stations until 1952, when the White Sox started having all games broadcast on <a href="/wiki/WCFL_(AM)" title="WCFL (AM)">WCFL</a> (1000).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Throughout this period of instability, one thing remained constant: the White Sox play-by-play announcer, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Elson" title="Bob Elson">Bob Elson</a>. Known as the "Commander", Elson was the voice of the Sox from 1929 until his departure from the club in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In 1979, he was the recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Frick_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Frick Award">Ford Frick Award</a>, and his profile is permanently on display in the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a>.\n</p><p>After the 1966 season, radio rights shifted from WCFL to <a href="/wiki/WMAQ_(AM)" title="WMAQ (AM)">WMAQ</a> (670). An <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> owned &amp; operated station until 1988 when <a href="/wiki/Westinghouse_Broadcasting" title="Westinghouse Broadcasting">Westinghouse Broadcasting</a> purchased it after NBC\'s withdrawal from radio, it was the home of the Sox until the 1996 season, outside of a team nadir in the early 70s where it was forced to <a href="/wiki/Brokered_programming" title="Brokered programming">broker time</a> on suburban <a href="/wiki/La_Grange,_Illinois" title="La Grange, Illinois">La Grange</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/WRDZ_(AM)" title="WRDZ (AM)">WTAQ</a> (1300) and <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Illinois" title="Evanston, Illinois">Evanston</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/WOJO" title="WOJO">WEAW-FM</a> (105.1) to have their play-by-play air in some form (though WEAW transmitted from the <a href="/wiki/875_North_Michigan_Avenue" title="875 North Michigan Avenue">John Hancock Center</a>, FM radio was not established as a band for sports play-by-play at the time)<sup id="cite_ref-cbmradio_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbmradio-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>, and a one-season contract on <a href="/wiki/WBBM_(AM)" title="WBBM (AM)">WBBM</a> (780) in 1981. After Elson\'s retirement in 1970, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Caray" title="Harry Caray">Harry Caray</a> began his tenure as the voice of the White Sox, on radio as well as on television. Although best remembered as a broadcaster for the rival Cubs, Caray was very popular with White Sox fans, pining for a "cold one" during broadcasts.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Caray would often broadcast from the stands, sitting at a table set up amidst the bleachers. It became a badge of honor among Sox fans to "Buy Harry a beer..." By game\'s end you\'d see a large stack of empty beer cups beside his microphone. This only endeared him to fans that much more. In fact, it was with the Sox that he started his tradition of leading the fans in the singing of <a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Out_To_The_Ballgame" class="mw-redirect" title="Take Me Out To The Ballgame">Take Me Out To The Ballgame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Caray, alongside color analyst <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Piersall" title="Jimmy Piersall">Jimmy Piersall</a>, was never afraid to criticize the Sox, which angered numerous Sox managers and players, notably <a href="/wiki/Bill_Melton" title="Bill Melton">Bill Melton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Tanner" title="Chuck Tanner">Chuck Tanner</a>. He left to succeed <a href="/wiki/Jack_Brickhouse" title="Jack Brickhouse">Jack Brickhouse</a> as the voice of the Cubs in 1981, where he became a national icon.\n</p><p>The White Sox shifted through several announcers in the 1980s, before hiring <a href="/wiki/John_Rooney_(sportscaster)" title="John Rooney (sportscaster)">John Rooney</a> as play-by-play announcer in 1989. In 1992, he was paired with color announcer <a href="/wiki/Ed_Farmer" title="Ed Farmer">Ed Farmer</a>. In 14 seasons together, the duo became a highly celebrated announcing team, even being ranked by <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a> as the top broadcasting team in the American League.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Starting with Rooney and Farmer\'s fifth season together, Sox games returned to the 1000 AM frequency for the first time in 30 years (now the <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Radio" title="ESPN Radio">ESPN owned &amp; operated</a> station <a href="/wiki/WMVP_(AM)" class="mw-redirect" title="WMVP (AM)">WMVP</a>). The last game on WMVP was Game 4 of the 2005 World Series, with the White Sox clinching their first World Series title in 88 years. That also was Rooney\'s last game with the Sox, as he left to join the radio broadcast team of the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>.\n</p><p>In 2006, radio broadcasts returned to 670, this time on the <a href="/wiki/Sports_radio" title="Sports radio">sports radio</a> station <a href="/wiki/WSCR" title="WSCR">WSCR</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/CBS_Radio" title="CBS Radio">CBS Radio</a> (WSCR took over the 670 frequency in August 2000 as part of a number of shifts among CBS Radio properties to meet market ownership caps). Ed Farmer became the play-by-play man after Rooney left, joined in the booth by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Singleton_(baseball)" title="Chris Singleton (baseball)">Chris Singleton</a> from 2006 to 2007 and then <a href="/wiki/Steve_Stone_(baseball)" title="Steve Stone (baseball)">Steve Stone</a> in 2008. In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Darrin_Jackson" title="Darrin Jackson">Darrin Jackson</a> became the color announcer for White Sox radio, where he remains today.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Farmer and Jackson were joined by pre-game/post-game host Chris Rogney\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox_Radio_Network" title="Chicago White Sox Radio Network">Chicago White Sox Radio Network</a> currently has 18 affiliates in 3 states.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> As of recently, White Sox games are also broadcast in Spanish with play-by-play announcer <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hector_Molina&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hector Molina (page does not exist)">Hector Molina</a> joined in the booth by Billy Russo.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Formerly broadcasting on <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Deportes_Radio" title="ESPN Deportes Radio">ESPN Deportes Radio</a> via <a href="/wiki/WEBG" title="WEBG">WNUA</a>, games are now broadcast in Spanish on <a href="/wiki/WRTO_(AM)" title="WRTO (AM)">WRTO</a> (1200).<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 2016 season, the play-by-play rights shifted to <a href="/wiki/Cumulus_Media" title="Cumulus Media">Cumulus Media</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/WLS_(AM)" title="WLS (AM)">WLS</a> (890) under a five-year deal, when WSCR acquired the rights to Cubs games after a one-year period on WBBM. However, by all counts, the deal was a disaster for the White Sox, as WLS\'s declining <a href="/wiki/Conservative_talk" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative talk">conservative talk</a> format, associated ratings, and management/personnel issues (including said hosts barely promoting the team and its games), and a signal that is weak in the northern suburbs and into <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a>, was not a good fit for the team. Cumulus also had voluminous financial issues, and by the start of 2018, looked to both file <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11_bankruptcy" class="mw-redirect" title="Chapter 11 bankruptcy">Chapter 11 bankruptcy</a> and get out of the play-by-play business entirely, both with local teams and nationally through their <a href="/wiki/NFL_on_Westwood_One_Sports" title="NFL on Westwood One Sports">Westwood One/NFL</a> deal.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbmradio_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbmradio-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The White Sox and <a href="/wiki/Tribune_Broadcasting" title="Tribune Broadcasting">Tribune Broadcasting</a> then announced a three-year deal for <a href="/wiki/WGN_(AM)" title="WGN (AM)">WGN Radio</a> to become the White Sox flagship as of February 14, 2018, just in time for <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">spring training</a>. Ed Farmer and Darrin Jackson will continue to be on play-by-play, with Andy Masur taking over pre-game/post-game duties.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>White Sox games appeared sporadically on television throughout the first half of the 20th century, most commonly announced by Jack Brickhouse on <a href="/wiki/WGN-TV" title="WGN-TV">WGN-TV</a> (channel 9). Starting in 1968, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Drees" title="Jack Drees">Jack Drees</a> took play-by-play duties as the Sox were broadcast on <a href="/wiki/WFLD" title="WFLD">WFLD</a> (channel 32).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> After 1972, Harry Caray (joined by Jimmy Piersall in 1977) began double duty as a TV and Radio announcer for the Sox, as broadcasts were moved to channel 44, <a href="/wiki/WSNS-TV" title="WSNS-TV">WSNS-TV</a>, from 1972 to 1980, followed by one year on WGN-TV.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a> became the play-by-play announcer in 1982, as the White Sox began splitting their broadcasts between WFLD and the new regional <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable television</a> network, <a href="/wiki/FSN_Chicago" title="FSN Chicago">Sportsvision</a>. Ahead of its time, Sportsvision had a chance to gain huge profits for the Sox. However, few people would subscribe to the channel after being used to free-to-air broadcasts for many years, along with Sportsvision being stunted by the city of Chicago\'s wiring for <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable television</a> taking much longer than many markets because of it being an area where over-the-air subscription services were still more popular, resulting in the franchise losing around $300,000 a month.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> While this was going on, every Cubs game was on WGN, with Harry Caray becoming the national icon he never was with the White Sox. The relatively easy near-national access to Cubs games versus Sox games in this era, combined with the popularity of Caray and the Cubs being owned by the <a href="/wiki/Tribune_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Tribune Company">Tribune Company</a>, is said by some to be the main cause of the Cubs\' advantage in popularity over the Sox.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hawk_Harrelson_2007_CROP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Hawk_Harrelson_2007_CROP.jpg/235px-Hawk_Harrelson_2007_CROP.jpg" width="235" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Hawk_Harrelson_2007_CROP.jpg/353px-Hawk_Harrelson_2007_CROP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Hawk_Harrelson_2007_CROP.jpg/470px-Hawk_Harrelson_2007_CROP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="560" data-file-height="396" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hawk_Harrelson_2007_CROP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harrelson in the broadcast booth in 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>Three major changes to White Sox broadcasting happened each year from 1989 to 1991: in 1989 with the city finally fully wired for cable service, Sportsvision was replaced by SportsChannel Chicago (itself eventually turning into <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Networks" title="Fox Sports Networks">Fox Sports Net</a> Chicago), which varied over its early years as a premium sports service and basic cable channel. In 1990, over-the-air broadcasts shifted back to WGN. And in 1991, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Harrelson" title="Ken Harrelson">Ken Harrelson</a> became the play by play announcer of the White Sox.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> One of the most polarizing figures in baseball, "Hawk" has been both adored and scorned for his emotive announcing style. His history of calling out umpires has earned him reprimands from the Commissioner\'s office, and he has been said to be the most biased announcer in baseball.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> However, Harrelson has said that he is proud of being "the biggest homer in baseball", saying that he is a White Sox fan like his viewers.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The team moved from FSN Chicago to the newly-launched <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports_Chicago" title="NBC Sports Chicago">NBC Sports Chicago</a> in March 2005, as Jerry Reinsdorf looked to control the rights for his team rather than sell rights to another party; Reinsdorf holds a 40% interest in the network, with 20% of that interest directly owned by the White Sox corporation.\n</p><p>Currently, White Sox local television broadcasts are split between two channels: the majority of games are broadcast on cable by NBC Sports Chicago, and remaining games are produced by <a href="/wiki/WGN_Sports" title="WGN Sports">WGN Sports</a> and are broadcast locally on <a href="/wiki/WGN-TV" title="WGN-TV">WGN-TV</a>. WGN games are also occasionally picked up by local stations in Illinois, Iowa, and Indiana. In the past, WGN games were broadcast nationally on the <a href="/wiki/WGN_America" title="WGN America">WGN America</a> superstation, but those broadcasts ended after the 2014 season as WGN America began its transition to a standard cable network.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> WGN Sports-produced White Sox games not carried by WGN-TV were carried by <a href="/wiki/WCIU-TV" title="WCIU-TV">WCIU-TV</a> (channel 26) until the 2015 season, when they moved to <a href="/wiki/MyNetworkTV" title="MyNetworkTV">MyNetworkTV</a> station <a href="/wiki/WPWR" class="mw-redirect" title="WPWR">WPWR</a> (channel 50).<sup id="cite_ref-trib-whitesoxwpwr_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trib-whitesoxwpwr-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> That arrangement ended on September 1, 2016 when WGN became an independent station.\n</p><p>Prior to 2016, the announcers were the same no matter where the games were broadcast: Harrelson provided play-by-play, and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Stone_(baseball)" title="Steve Stone (baseball)">Steve Stone</a> provided color analysis since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Games that are broadcast on NBC Sports Chicago feature pregame and postgame shows, hosted by Chuck Garfein with analysis from <a href="/wiki/Bill_Melton" title="Bill Melton">Bill Melton</a> and occasionally <a href="/wiki/Frank_Thomas_(designated_hitter)" title="Frank Thomas (designated hitter)">Frank Thomas</a>. In 2016, the team announced an official split of the play-by-play duties, with Harrelson calling road games and the <a href="/wiki/Crosstown_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Crosstown Series">Crosstown Series</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Benetti" title="Jason Benetti">Jason Benetti</a> calling home games.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the team announced that the 2018 season will be Harrelson\'s final in the booth. He will call 20 games over the course of the season, after which Benetti will take over full-time play-by-play duties.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/wiki/Luis_Aparicio" title="Luis Aparicio">Luis Aparicio</a>\'s number 11 was issued at his request for the 2010 and 2011 seasons for 11 time <a href="/wiki/Rawlings_Gold_Glove_Award" title="Rawlings Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove</a> winner shortstop <a href="/wiki/Omar_Vizquel" title="Omar Vizquel">Omar Vizquel</a> (because number 13 was used by manager <a href="/wiki/Ozzie_Guill%C3%A9n" title="Ozzie Guill\xc3\xa9n">Ozzie Guill\xc3\xa9n</a>; Vizquel, like Aparicio and Guillen, play(ed) shortstop and all share a common Venezuelan heritage).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Baines" title="Harold Baines">Harold Baines</a> had his number 3 retired in 1989; it has since been \'unretired\' 3 times in each of his subsequent returns.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Out_of_circulation.2C_but_not_retired"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Out_of_circulation,_but_not_retired">Out of circulation, but not retired</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Out of circulation, but not retired">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><b>6:</b> Since <a href="/wiki/Charley_Lau" title="Charley Lau">Charley Lau</a>\'s death in 1984, no White Sox player or coach (except Lau disciple <a href="/wiki/Walt_Hriniak" title="Walt Hriniak">Walt Hriniak</a>, the Chicago White Sox\' hitting coach from 1989 to 1995) has worn his number 6 jersey, although it has not been officially retired.</li>\n<li><b>13:</b> Since <a href="/wiki/Ozzie_Guill%C3%A9n" title="Ozzie Guill\xc3\xa9n">Ozzie Guill\xc3\xa9n</a> left as manager of the White Sox, no Sox player or coach has worn his number 13 jersey, although it is not officially retired.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball_Hall_of_Famers">Baseball Hall of Famers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span href="/wiki/Glendale,_Arizona" title="Glendale, Arizona">Glendale, Arizona</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Silver_Chalice_subsidiary">Silver Chalice subsidiary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Silver Chalice subsidiary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Silver Chalice is a digital and media investment subsidiary of the White Sox with Brooks Boyers as CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-ct_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Silver Chalice was co-founded by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Reinsdorf" title="Jerry Reinsdorf">Jerry Reinsdorf</a>, White Sox executive Brooks Boyer, Jason Coyle and John Burris in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-ct_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ct0_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct0-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Chalice has since partnered with IMG on <a href="/wiki/Campus_Insiders" title="Campus Insiders">Campus Insiders</a>, a college sports digital channel.<sup id="cite_ref-ct_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The company also invested in <a href="/wiki/120_Sports" title="120 Sports">120 Sports</a>, a digital sports channel, that launched in June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ct0_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct0-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> These efforts have since been merged with <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Broadcasting_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Sinclair Broadcasting Group">Sinclair Broadcasting Group</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/American_Sports_Network" title="American Sports Network">American Sports Network</a> into the new multi-platform network <a href="/wiki/Stadium_(sports_network)" title="Stadium (sports network)">Stadium</a> as of September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_White_Sox&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The team\'s official colors are black and silver, according to the team\'s mascot (Southpaw)\'s official website.<sup id="cite_ref-AboutSouthpaw_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AboutSouthpaw-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
